true;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    if (unused_outputs > 0) {\n      for (int i = 0; i < n->num_outputs(); ++i) {\n        if (!outputs_required[i]) {\n For robust error handling in C++, adopt practices such as using exceptions for error reporting, validating inputs, and implementing logging mechanisms to capture errors. Ensure that your code checks for potential failure points and handles them gracefully to prevent silent failures. Additionally, consider using smart pointers and RAII (Resource Acquisition Is Initialization) to manage resources effectively.\n\n3. Safer alternatives to `strcpy` and `sprintf` in C++ include using `strncpy` and `snprintf`, which allow you to specify buffer sizes to prevent overflow. Libraries like the Safe C String Library (SafeStr) and Microsoft's Strsafe.h also provide safer string-handling functions. These alternatives help mitigate buffer overflow vulnerabilities by enforcing length checks.", additional_kwargs={}, response_metadata={}, name='Rag_subgraph')], 'sender': 'Rag_subgraph', 'target': 'Prompter_node', 'rag_calls': 4}, 'triggers': ['branch:Rag_subgraph:router:Prompter_node']}}
